On the other hand, I would advise you, Caspian, not to go giving out any more of Mistborn’s old school things. If any more of them find their way into innocent hands, I think Arthur Brunswick, for one, will make sure they are traced back to you. …”

Caspian Mortem stood for a moment, and Eli distinctly saw his right hand twitch as though he was longing to reach for his wand. Instead, he turned to his house-elf.

“We’re going, Nobby!”

He wrenched open the door and as the elf came hurrying up to him, he kicked him right through it. They could hear Nobby squealing with pain all the way along the corridor. Eli stood for a moment, thinking hard. Then it came to him —

“Professor Starling,” he said hurriedly. “Can I give that diary back to Mr. Mortem, please?”

“Certainly, Eli,” said Starling calmly. “But hurry. The feast, remember. …”

Eli grabbed the diary and dashed out of the office. He could hear Nobby’s squeals of pain receding around the corner. Quickly, wondering if this plan could possibly work, Eli took off one of his shoes, pulled off his slimy, filthy sock, and stuffed the diary into it. Then he ran down the dark corridor.

He caught up with them at the top of the stairs.

“Mr. Mortem,” he gasped, skidding to a halt, “I’ve got something for you —”

And he forced the smelly sock into Caspian Mortem’s hand.

“What the — ?”

Mr. Mortem ripped the sock off the diary, threw it aside, then looked furiously from the ruined book to Eli.

“You’ll meet the same sticky end as your parents one of these days, Eli Ember,” he said softly. “They were meddlesome fools, too.”

He turned to go.

“Come, Nobby. I said, come.”

But Nobby didn’t move. He was holding up Eli’s disgusting, slimy sock, and looking at it as though it were a priceless treasure.

“Master has given a sock,” said the elf in wonderment. “Master gave it to Nobby.”

“What’s that?” spat Mr. Mortem. “What did you say?”

“Got a sock,” said Nobby in disbelief. “Master threw it, and Nobby caught it, and Nobby — Nobby is free.”

Caspian Mortem stood frozen, staring at the elf. Then he lunged at Eli.

“You’ve lost me my servant, boy!”

But Nobby shouted, “You shall not harm Eli Ember!”

There was a loud bang, and Mr. Mortem was thrown backward. He crashed down the stairs, three at a time, landing in a crumpled heap on the landing below. He got up, his face livid, and pulled out his wand, but Nobby raised a long, threatening finger.

“You shall go now,” he said fiercely, pointing down at Mr. Mortem. “You shall not touch Eli Ember. You shall go now.”

Caspian Mortem had no choice. With a last, incensed stare at the pair of them, he swung his cloak around him and hurried out of sight.

“Eli Ember freed Nobby!” said the elf shrilly, gazing up at Eli, moonlight from the nearest window reflected in his orb-like eyes. “Eli Ember set Nobby free!”

“Least I could do, Nobby,” said Eli, grinning. “Just promise never to try and save my life again.”

The elf’s ugly brown face split suddenly into a wide, toothy smile.

“I’ve just got one question, Nobby,” said Eli as Nobby pulled on Eli’s sock with shaking hands. “You told me all this had nothing to do with He-Who-Must-Not-Be-Named, remember? Well —”

“It was a clue, sir,” said Nobby, his eyes widening, as though this was obvious. “Was giving you a clue. The Dark Lord, before he changed his name, could be freely named, you see?”

“Right,” said Eli weakly. “Well, I’d better go. There’s a feast, and my friend Isla should be awake by now. …”

Nobby threw his arms around Eli’s middle and hugged him.

“Eli Ember is greater by far than Nobby knew!” he sobbed. “Farewell, Eli Ember!”

And with a final loud crack, Nobby disappeared.



Eli had been to several Hogwarts feasts, but never one quite like this. Everybody was in their pajamas, and the celebration lasted all night. Eli didn’t know whether the best bit was Isla running toward him, screaming “You solved it! You solved it!” or Justin hurrying over from the Hufflepuff table to wring his hand and apologize endlessly for suspecting him, or Griff turning up at half past three, cuffing Eli and Leo so hard on the shoulders that they were knocked into their plates of trifle, or his and Leo’s four hundred points for Gryffindor securing the House Cup for the second year running, or Professor Falconer standing up to tell them all that the exams had been canceled as a school treat (“Oh, no!” said Isla), or Starling announcing that, unfortunately, Professor Bright would be unable to return next year, owing to the fact that he needed to go away and get his memory back. Quite a few of the teachers joined in the cheering that greeted this news.

“Shame,” said Leo, helping himself to a jam doughnut. “He was starting to grow on me.”



The rest of the final term passed in a haze of blazing sunshine. Hogwarts was back to normal with only a few, small differences — Defense Against the Dark Arts classes were canceled (“but we’ve had plenty of practice at that anyway,” Leo told a disgruntled Isla) and Caspian Mortem had been sacked as a school governor. Jasper was no longer strutting around the school as though he owned the place. On the contrary, he looked resentful and sulky. On the other hand, Lila Brunswick was perfectly happy again.

Too soon, it was time for the journey home on the Hogwarts Express. Eli, Leo, Isla, Felix, Aiden, and Lila got a compartment to themselves. They made the most of the last few hours in which they were allowed to do magic before the holidays. They played Exploding Snap, set off the very last of Felix and Aiden’s Filibuster fireworks, and practiced disarming each other by magic. Eli was getting very good at it.

They were almost at King’s Cross when Eli remembered something.

“Lila — what did you see Evan doing, that he didn’t want you to tell anyone?”

“Oh, that,” said Lila, giggling. “Well — Evan’s got a girlfriend.”

Felix dropped a stack of books on Aiden’s head.

“What?”

“It’s that Ravenclaw prefect, Penelope Springwater,” said Lila. “That’s who he was writing to all last summer. He’s been meeting her all over the school in secret. I walked in on them kissing in an empty classroom one day. He was so upset when she was — you know — attacked. You won’t tease him, will you?” she added anxiously.

“Wouldn’t dream of it,” said Felix, who was looking like his birthday had come early.

“Definitely not,” said Aiden, sniggering.

The Hogwarts Express slowed and finally stopped.

Eli pulled out his quill and a bit of parchment and turned to Leo and Isla.

“This is called a telephone number,” he told Leo, scribbling it twice, tearing the parchment in two, and handing it to them. “I told your dad how to use a telephone last summer — he’ll know. Call me at the Powells’, okay? I can’t stand another two months with only Carson to talk to. …”

“Your aunt and uncle will be proud, though, won’t they?” said Isla as they got off the train and joined the crowd thronging toward the enchanted barrier. “When they hear what you did this year?

“Proud?” said Eli. “Are you crazy? All those times I could’ve died, and I didn’t manage it? They’ll be furious. …”

And together they walked back through the gateway to the Muggle world.
